              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer578624600">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4653875803334098615">This is the first of Heinlein's books I've come across. An intriguing set up, but with far to little focus applied to the last 7 chapters. I felt as though I had an in depth experience with the first portion of the book, and suddenly was reading the sparknotes for the later half of the novel. The book was a jarring mass of implied plot lines and then unaddressed instances. At the end of the book the only conclusions I came away with were strictly based on my own guesses and speculation at how th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4653875803334098615">This is the first of Heinlein's books I've come across. An intriguing set up, but with far to little focus applied to the last 7 chapters. I felt as though I had an in depth experience with the first portion of the book, and suddenly was reading the sparknotes for the later half of the novel. The book was a jarring mass of implied plot lines and then unaddressed instances. At the end of the book the only conclusions I came away with were strictly based on my own guesses and speculation at how things 'might' have panned out. It drives me crazy when writers do this. I had the distinct impression that the end was a set up for further explication (it wouldn't have taken much to wrap stuff up). I was left thinking that the writer was out of things to say. Wouldn't recommend this book, though the characters are memorable and charming in a hazy, inconclusive sort of way.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17281437433848239977">This is another of my favorite Heinlein novels. It has characteristics of the juveniles, centering on a young man coming of age, but has more of the plot structure typical of more mature novels.<br /><br />In another sense, it is a series of short stories following a (to start) young boy who is a slave, then a freedman beggar in the streets, then a spaceman free trader and finally one of the richest men in the galaxy. At each step he takes what he learns to be better in the roles to come. The progression is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17281437433848239977">This is another of my favorite Heinlein novels. It has characteristics of the juveniles, centering on a young man coming of age, but has more of the plot structure typical of more mature novels.<br /><br />In another sense, it is a series of short stories following a (to start) young boy who is a slave, then a freedman beggar in the streets, then a spaceman free trader and finally one of the richest men in the galaxy. At each step he takes what he learns to be better in the roles to come. The progression is more varied than most would experience, but it says a lot about the progression through various stages of our life.<br /><br />I wasn't sure if this one would work as well for the kids, but it turns out to have been a great choice for them, too!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/85153611?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 15, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3157632-ouranosaurus" class="user" title="Ouranosaurus">Ouranosaurus</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16689.Citizen_of_the_Galaxy" title="Paperback 9781416505525" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer85153611'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer85153611">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8824431217149296443">My favourite Heinlein book is an odd one. It's the last of his "juveniles," and intended for a slightly older audience than most of the books in that sequence. These days it would probably be shelved as YA.<br /><br />Heinlein almost drops his normal attitude of total certainty and pulls back a bit, allowing his protagonist, Thorby, to find his way through several different societies. From life as a slave, to a free beggar, to a career as a spy, space ship crew member, and finally lost heir, every society i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8824431217149296443">My favourite Heinlein book is an odd one. It's the last of his "juveniles," and intended for a slightly older audience than most of the books in that sequence. These days it would probably be shelved as YA.<br /><br />Heinlein almost drops his normal attitude of total certainty and pulls back a bit, allowing his protagonist, Thorby, to find his way through several different societies. From life as a slave, to a free beggar, to a career as a spy, space ship crew member, and finally lost heir, every society in which Thorby moves has its own rules, its own pitfalls. Except for the institution of slavery, Heinlein condemns nothing, leaving it up to the reader to decide what is good and bad about each.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8824431217149296443">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_456290926">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/456290926" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9764974-rebecca" class="left imgcol" title="Rebecca"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1357380998p2/9764974.jpg" alt="Rebecca" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/456290926?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 14, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9764974-rebecca" class="user" title="Rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16689.Citizen_of_the_Galaxy" title="Paperback 9781416505525" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer456290926">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18305046140445845666">Citizen of the Galaxy is one of my very favorite books of all time. It gets a reread at least once a year. Thorby starts out this book as a slave being auctioned. He is bought by the beggar, Baslim the Cripple. As the book progresses, we along with Thorby, realize that Baslim is not what he seems. This book explores what it means to be human, the inhumanity of slavery and the resilience of the human spirit. It's very well written, entertaining, with wonderful characters and worlds. While I have</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18305046140445845666">Citizen of the Galaxy is one of my very favorite books of all time. It gets a reread at least once a year. Thorby starts out this book as a slave being auctioned. He is bought by the beggar, Baslim the Cripple. As the book progresses, we along with Thorby, realize that Baslim is not what he seems. This book explores what it means to be human, the inhumanity of slavery and the resilience of the human spirit. It's very well written, entertaining, with wonderful characters and worlds. While I have issues with a lot of Heinlein's novels for adults, his YA books are by and large wonderful. Highly recommended for anyone of any age.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18305046140445845666">...more</a>

          </span>

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lKTuVCVU6LlPoEYKqWTDRWZaPCEWX84+EuiB5+XUbrvxcNGH14b8Q8N4MrHXBSX3L63/OF+CiZR44YR1KUGY/g==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/205.Robert_A_Heinlein">About Robert A. Heinlein</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/205.Robert_A_Heinlein"><img alt="205" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1192826560p2/205.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14508888599747001903">Robert Anson Heinlein was an American novelist and science fiction writer. Often called "the dean of science fiction writers", he is one of the most popular, influential, and controversial authors of "hard science fiction". <br /><br />He set a high standard for science and engineering plausibility and helped to raise the genre's standards of literary quality. He was the first SF writer to break into mainstre</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14508888599747001903">Robert Anson Heinlein was an American novelist and science fiction writer. Often called "the dean of science fiction writers", he is one of the most popular, influential, and controversial authors of "hard science fiction". <br /><br />He set a high standard for science and engineering plausibility and helped to raise the genre's standards of literary quality. He was the first SF writer to break into mainstream, general magazines such as "The Saturday Evening Post", in the late 1940s. He was also among the first authors of bestselling, novel-length science fiction in the modern, mass-market era. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14508888599747001903">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/205.Robert_A_Heinlein" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Robert A. Heinlein...</a>

It has since been in print for 50 years in paperback, and now returns to hardcover for a new generation. Travel to other planets is a reality, and with overpopulation stretching the resources of Earth, the necessity to find habitable worlds is growing ever more urgent. With no time to wait years for communication between slower-than-light spaceships and home, the Long Range Foundation explores an unlikely solution--human telepathy.Identical twins Tom and Pat are enlisted to be the human radios that will keep the ships in contact with Earth. The only problem is that one of them has to stay behind, and that one will grow old while the other explores the depths of space.Always a master of insight into the human consequences of future technologies, this is one of Heinlein\'s triumphs.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"12106023049648403234\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent($(this));; return false;\"&gt;...more&lt;\/a&gt;\n\n         script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]&gt;
</script>
